"""Paged attention decode kernel -- CUDA C++ two-pass with GQA sharing.

Pass 1: CUDA kernel tiles the sequence across blocks. Each block handles one
(batch, kv_head, tile). KV is loaded cooperatively into shared memory and shared
across all GROUP warps (one per query head). Partial softmax stats are written
to global scratch buffers.

Pass 2: PyTorch vectorized reduction merges the per-tile partials into the
final attention output.
"""
import math

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

OP_TYPE = "attention"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]

BATCH = 8
NUM_HEADS = 32
NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
HEAD_DIM = 128
SEQ_LEN = 1024
PAGE_SIZE = 16

CUDA_SRC = r"""
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda.h>
#include <cuda_bf16.h>
#include <cfloat>
#include <cmath>

__device__ __forceinline__ float warp_reduce_sum(float v) {
    #pragma unroll
    for (int m = 16; m > 0; m >>= 1)
        v += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, v, m);
    return v;
}

template <int HEAD_DIM>
__global__ void paged_attn_gqa_kernel(
    const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ query,
    const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ kv_cache,
    const int* __restrict__ block_table,
    const int* __restrict__ seq_lens,
    float* __restrict__ partial_m,
    float* __restrict__ partial_l,
    float* __restrict__ partial_o,
    const int H, const int Hkv, const int P,
    const int max_pages, const int group_size,
    const int pages_per_tile, const int num_tiles
) {
    extern __shared__ __nv_bfloat16 smem_kv[];
    auto* smem_k = smem_kv;
    auto* smem_v = smem_kv + P * HEAD_DIM;

    const int wid  = threadIdx.x / 32;
    const int lane = threadIdx.x % 32;
    const int tid  = threadIdx.x;
    const int nthreads = blockDim.x;

    const int pid  = blockIdx.x;
    const int tile = pid % num_tiles;
    const int bkv  = pid / num_tiles;
    const int b    = bkv / Hkv;
    const int hkv  = bkv % Hkv;
    const int h    = hkv * group_size + wid;
    const int bh   = b * H + h;

    const int seq_len = seq_lens[b];
    constexpr int E = HEAD_DIM / 32;
    const bool active = (wid < group_size) && (h < H) && (seq_len > 0);

    if (!active) {
        if (h < H) {
            if (lane == 0) {
                partial_m[bh * num_tiles + tile] = -FLT_MAX;
                partial_l[bh * num_tiles + tile] = 0.f;
            }
            for (int i = 0; i < E; i++)
                partial_o[(bh * num_tiles + tile) * HEAD_DIM + lane * E + i] = 0.f;
        }
        return;
    }

    const float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)HEAD_DIM);

    const auto* qbase = query + (size_t)bh * HEAD_DIM;
    float q[E];
    for (int i = 0; i < E; i++)
        q[i] = __bfloat162float(qbase[lane * E + i]);

    const int total_pages = (seq_len + P - 1) / P;
    const int ts = tile * pages_per_tile;
    const int te = min(ts + pages_per_tile, total_pages);

    float mi = -FLT_MAX;
    float li = 0.f;
    float oi[E];
    for (int i = 0; i < E; i++) oi[i] = 0.f;

    const size_t sb = (size_t)P * Hkv * HEAD_DIM * 2;
    const size_t ss = (size_t)Hkv * HEAD_DIM * 2;
    const size_t sh = (size_t)HEAD_DIM * 2;

    for (int p = ts; p < te; p++) {
        const int phys = block_table[b * max_pages + p];
        const auto* kb = kv_cache + (size_t)phys * sb + (size_t)hkv * sh;
        const int ps = p * P;
        const int pe = (ps + P < seq_len) ? ps + P : seq_len;
        const int valid = pe - ps;
        const int nk = valid * HEAD_DIM;

        for (int idx = tid; idx < nk; idx += nthreads) {
            int s = idx / HEAD_DIM, d = idx % HEAD_DIM;
            smem_k[idx] = kb[(size_t)s * ss + d];
        }
        for (int idx = tid; idx < nk; idx += nthreads) {
            int s = idx / HEAD_DIM, d = idx % HEAD_DIM;
            smem_v[idx] = kb[(size_t)s * ss + HEAD_DIM + d];
        }
        __syncthreads();

        for (int s = 0; s < valid; s++) {
            float dot = 0.f;
            for (int i = 0; i < E; i++) {
                float ki = __bfloat162float(smem_k[s * HEAD_DIM + lane * E + i]);
                dot += q[i] * ki;
            }
            float score = warp_reduce_sum(dot) * scale;
            float mn = fmaxf(mi, score);
            float cg = expf(mi - mn);
            float es = expf(score - mn);
            li = li * cg + es;
            for (int i = 0; i < E; i++) oi[i] *= cg;
            for (int i = 0; i < E; i++) {
                float vi = __bfloat162float(smem_v[s * HEAD_DIM + lane * E + i]);
                oi[i] += es * vi;
            }
            mi = mn;
        }
        __syncthreads();
    }

    if (lane == 0) {
        partial_m[bh * num_tiles + tile] = mi;
        partial_l[bh * num_tiles + tile] = li;
    }
    for (int i = 0; i < E; i++)
        partial_o[(bh * num_tiles + tile) * HEAD_DIM + lane * E + i] = oi[i];
}

void gqa_fwd(
    torch::Tensor query, torch::Tensor kv_cache,
    torch::Tensor bt, torch::Tensor sl,
    torch::Tensor pm, torch::Tensor pl, torch::Tensor po,
    int64_t hkv_, int64_t P_, int64_t GS_, int64_t NT_, int64_t PP_
) {
    const int B  = query.size(0);
    const int H  = query.size(1);
    const int D  = query.size(2);
    const int Hkv = (int)hkv_;
    const int P  = (int)P_;
    const int GS = (int)GS_;
    const int NT = (int)NT_;
    const int PP = (int)PP_;
    const int MP = bt.size(1);

    const int grid_sz = B * Hkv * NT;
    const int blk_sz  = GS * 32;
    const size_t smem = 2 * P * D * sizeof(at::BFloat16);

    auto qp  = reinterpret_cast<const __nv_bfloat16*>(query.data_ptr<at::BFloat16>());
    auto kvp = reinterpret_cast<const __nv_bfloat16*>(kv_cache.data_ptr<at::BFloat16>());
    auto btp = bt.data_ptr<int32_t>();
    auto slp = sl.data_ptr<int32_t>();

    if (D == 128)
        paged_attn_gqa_kernel<128><<<grid_sz, blk_sz, smem>>>(
            qp, kvp, btp, slp,
            pm.data_ptr<float>(), pl.data_ptr<float>(), po.data_ptr<float>(),
            H, Hkv, P, MP, GS, PP, NT);
    else
        paged_attn_gqa_kernel<64><<<grid_sz, blk_sz, smem>>>(
            qp, kvp, btp, slp,
            pm.data_ptr<float>(), pl.data_ptr<float>(), po.data_ptr<float>(),
            H, Hkv, P, MP, GS, PP, NT);

    auto err = cudaGetLastError();
    if (err != cudaSuccess)
        throw std::runtime_error(cudaGetErrorString(err));
}
"""

_mod = None

def _get_mod():
    global _mod
    if _mod is None:
        _mod = load_inline(
            name="paged_attn_gqa",
            cpp_sources=(
                "#include <torch/extension.h>\n"
                "void gqa_fwd(torch::Tensor,torch::Tensor,torch::Tensor,torch::Tensor,"
                "torch::Tensor,torch::Tensor,torch::Tensor,"
                "int64_t,int64_t,int64_t,int64_t,int64_t);\n"
            ),
            cuda_sources=CUDA_SRC,
            functions=["gqa_fwd"],
            extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "-std=c++17"],
            verbose=False,
        )
    return _mod


class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, batch, num_heads, num_kv_heads, head_dim, seq_len, page_size):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
        self.register_buffer(
            "_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False
        )

    def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens):
        B, H, D = query.shape
        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
        P = self.page_size
        GS = self.group_size

        max_sl = seq_lens.max().item()
        max_pages = (max_sl + P - 1) // P
        NT = max(1, min(64, -(-max_pages // 4)))  # at least 4 tiles per page chunk
        NT = max(NT, -(-512 // max(1, B * Hkv)))  # at least 512 blocks
        NT = min(NT, 64)
        ppt = -(-max_pages // NT)  # ceil div

        BH = B * H
        pm = torch.empty(BH, NT, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)
        pl = torch.empty(BH, NT, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)
        po = torch.empty(BH, NT, D, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)

        _get_mod().gqa_fwd(
            query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens,
            pm, pl, po, Hkv, P, GS, NT, ppt,
        )

        # Reduction: merge per-tile partial softmax stats
        m_global = pm.max(dim=1).values                  # (BH,)
        corr = torch.exp(pm - m_global.unsqueeze(1))     # (BH, NT)
        l_global = (pl * corr).sum(dim=1)                # (BH,)
        o_global = (po * corr.unsqueeze(2)).sum(dim=1)   # (BH, D)
        out = (o_global / l_global.unsqueeze(1)).to(torch.bfloat16)
        return out.reshape(B, H, D)


def get_inputs():
    B = BATCH; H = NUM_HEADS; Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
    D = HEAD_DIM; L = SEQ_LEN; P = PAGE_SIZE
    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)
    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    perm = (
        torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq]
        .reshape(B, pages_per_seq)
        .int()
    )
    block_table = perm.contiguous()
    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)
    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]

stdout (5623 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	"""Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
2	
3	Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
4	and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
5	a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
6	
7	The reference performs the slow path:
8	  1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
9	  2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).
10	  3. Manual softmax(QK^T / sqrt(d)) @ V in fp32, cast back to bf16.
11	
12	This avoids torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention (which is on the
13	forbidden list) so the agent cannot dispatch through SDPA either.
14	"""
15	import math
16	
17	import torch
18	import torch.nn as nn
19	
20	OP_TYPE = "attention"
21	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
22	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
23	
24	
25	# --- Shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py from shapes.py) ----
26	BATCH = 8
27	NUM_HEADS = 32
28	NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
29	HEAD_DIM = 128
30	SEQ_LEN = 1024
31	PAGE_SIZE = 16
32	
33	
34	class Model(nn.Module):
35	    """Single-query paged attention decode.
36	
37	    Forward inputs (all on device):
38	      query:       (batch, num_heads, head_dim)               bf16
39	      kv_cache:    (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)
40	                   Layout: last dim packs [K | V] so a single gather pulls both.
4

... (4123 more chars)
tool
stdout (981 chars)
1	"""Shape sweep for paged attention decode.
2	
3	Mix targets:
4	  - small batch / long context (Llama-3 8B-style decode)
5	  - large batch / medium context (server batched decode)
6	  - GQA wide ratio (Llama-3 70B: 64 heads / 8 kv-heads)
7	  - non-power-of-2 seq_len (forces predicated tail handling)
8	  - head_dim=64 small-head case
9	"""

7	# Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.

Now I have a clear picture of the problem. Let me understand the key aspects: 1. **Paged attention decode** - single query per batch element attending over KV cache stored in pages 2. **KV cache layout**: `(num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)` where last dim packs [K|V] 3. **GQA**: num_heads can be > num_kv_heads, need to repeat KV heads 4. **Shapes**: 5 shapes with varying batch, heads, head_dim, seq_len (including non-power-of-2) 5. **Tolerance**: 0.02 atol/rtol on bf16 6. **Memory-bound**: regime is "memory", so bandwidth utilization is the key metric 7. **Peak bandwidth**: 1.8 TB/s GDDR7 on RTX PRO 6000 For a decode kernel, the key bottleneck is streaming the KV cache from DRAM. The QK^T and AV computations are memory-bound since seq_len is small-ish (1K-4K) relative to head_dim=128. Let me think about the implementation approach: For a paged attention decode kernel in CUDA: **Approach: CUDA C++ via load_inline** The kernel should: 1. Each thread block handles one (batch, query_head) pair 2. Load Q for that head into registers/shared memory 3. Stream through KV pages, computing QK^T scores with online softmax 4. Maintain running sum and output accumulator For GQA: each KV head serves `group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads` query heads. So we can have thread blocks for each (batch, query_head). **Tiling strategy for decode attention:** For each (batch, query_head): - Q is (D,) - fits in registers easily (128 bf16 = 256 bytes for D=128) - Need to iterate over L tokens in KV cache - For each token, load K[D] and V[D], compute q·k, update running softmax and output The online softmax algorithm (FlashAttention-style): - Maintain running max, running sum, running output - For each new block of K/V: - Load K, V from paged cache - Compute scores = Q @ K^T - Update running max -> rescale previous accumulations - Update running sum and output Since this is decode (single query token), the Q matrix is tiny. The main work is streaming K and V through. **Implementation plan:** 1. Use CUDA C++ via `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline` 2. One thread block per (batch, query_head) pair 3. Use shared memory for Q, and iterate over KV pages 4. Online softmax for numerical stability 5. Handle page boundaries and seq_len masking Let me think about the thread/block mapping more carefully: For shape 1: B=8, H=32, Hkv=8, D=128, L=1024 - 8 * 32 = 256 thread blocks - Each block processes one (b, h) pair - Within each block, we need to process L=1024 tokens For shape 2: B=32, H=32, Hkv=8, D=128, L=2048 - 32 * 32 = 1024 thread blocks For shape 3: B=4, H=64, Hkv=8, D=128, L=4096 - 4 * 64 = 256 thread blocks For shape 4: B=16, H=32, Hkv=8, D=128, L=1535 - 16 * 32 = 512 thread blocks For shape 5: B=8, H=16, Hkv=4, D=64, L=2000 - 8 * 16 = 128 thread blocks Thread block size: 128 or 256 threads per block seems reasonable. For the KV access pattern: - Each thread block for (b, h) needs to map h to the correct kv_head: kv_h = h / group_size - Then iterate over pages for batch element b, loading K and V for kv_head - Page table: block_table[b, page_idx] gives the page number in kv_cache Let me think about the tiling within a thread block: For D=128 (bf16): - Each K row is 128 * 2 = 256 bytes - Each V row is 128 * 2 = 256 bytes - So each K/V pair for one token is 512 bytes For a block of `BLOCK_SIZE` tokens: - K: BLOCK_SIZE * 256 bytes - V: BLOCK_SIZE * 256 bytes With 256 threads, each thread can process multiple tokens. Actually, let me think about this differently. The key insight for decode is: 1. Q is (H, D) but we only look at one head per thread block: just D values 2. For each token position l, we compute score[h, l] = Q[h, :] . K[l, kv_h, :] / sqrt(D) 3. Then softmax over l, then weighted sum of V So the computation per (b, h) is: - Stream through L tokens - For each token: load K[D] and V[D], dot product Q with K, accumulate - After all tokens: apply softmax, multiply by V Using online softmax (FlashAttention trick): ``` m_i = -inf l_i = 0 O_i = 0 for each block j of KV: s_j = Q @ K_j^T / sqrt(D) # vector of scores m_new = max(m_i, max(s_j)) l_new = l_i * exp(m_i - m_new) + sum(exp(s_j - m_new)) O_new = O_i * (l_i * exp(m_i - m_new) / l_new) + sum(exp(s_j - m_new) / l_new * V_j) m_i = m_new l_i = l_new O_i = O_new ``` This is the standard online softmax approach. Now, for the CUDA implementation: **Thread mapping within a block:** Option A: Each thread handles multiple tokens sequentially - Thread block has blockDim.x threads - Token iteration: for l in range(tid, L, blockDim.x) - Each thread loads its own K[l] and V[l], computes dot product with Q - Need reduction for the dot product (Q is D-dimensional) Wait, this doesn't quite work because Q is D-dimensional and each thread would need all D values of Q to compute the dot product. Better approach: **Warp-level approach:** - Use warps to handle the head dimension - Each warp processes one token position at a time - Within a warp, threads cooperate on the D-dimensional dot product For D=128, a warp of 32 threads: each thread handles 128/32 = 4 elements of the dot product. **Or even simpler:** For D=128 bf16, we can load Q into shared memory (256 bytes). Then each thread processes one or more token positions: - Load K[l, :] from global memory (256 bytes) - Compute dot product with Q in registers - Accumulate score - Later, load V[l, :] and accumulate weighted sum But this means each thread does a full D-wide dot product... for D=128 bf16, that's 128 multiply-adds per token. With 128 threads and L=1024, each thread handles 8 tokens. That's fine. Actually wait, we should think about memory access patterns. Each thread loading K[l, :] independently would result in poor memory coalescing. Let me reconsider. **Better: Process tokens in blocks** Process BLOCK_SIZE tokens at a time within the thread block: - Cooperatively load a block of K values into shared memory - Each thread computes a subset of the QK dot products - Use shared memory for V block too - Update running softmax statistics Let me think about this more carefully for coalescing... The KV cache is (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2). For a given kv_head hkv, accessing K for token l within page p: - page p = block_table[b, l / page_size] - offset within page = l % page_size - K = kv_cache[p, offset, hkv, :D] - V = kv_cache[p, offset, hkv, D:] The stride pattern: accessing K[l, :] for fixed l means accessing consecutive elements in the last dimension - that's nicely coalesced! So if we have a warp read K[l, hkv, :] (128 bf16 values = 256 bytes), 32 threads each read 4 bf16 values. That's coalesced since the values are consecutive. Let me design the kernel: ```cpp // Grid: (batch * num_heads, 1, 1) // Block: (BLOCK_SIZE_THREADS, 1, 1) // Each block handles one (batch_idx, head_idx) pair // Within the block, threads cooperate to: // 1. Load Q into shared memory // 2. Iterate over pages in the KV cache // 3. For each page, process tokens cooperatively // 4. Maintain online softmax accumulators ``` Actually, let me think about a cleaner design. For decode attention, a popular approach is: - 1 warp per (batch, head) pair - Multiple warps per block (e.g., 4-8 warps) - Each warp processes one (batch, head) independently - This gives good occupancy With warp per (b, h): - 32 threads per warp - Q is in shared memory (or registers, since it's replicated per warp) - Each thread loads 128/32 = 4 elements of Q into registers - Iterate over tokens: for each token, cooperatively load K and V - 32 threads load 128 bf16 = 256 bytes, perfectly coalesced - Each thread has 4 elements of Q, 4 elements of K -> partial dot product - Warp reduce to get full dot product (score) - Then cooperatively load V, do weighted accumulation This is very clean. Let me go with this approach. **Detailed warp-level design:** ``` For each warp (handling batch b, query head h): kv_h = h / group_size // Load Q[h, :] into registers q_local[4] = Q[b, h, tid*4 : tid*4+4] // each thread loads 4 bf16 // Convert Q to float for accumulation qf[4] = float(q_local[4]) // Online softmax accumulators (per warp, in thread 0 or all threads) running_max = -inf running_sum = 0 o_acc[4] = {0} // output accumulator // Iterate over tokens for l in range(seq_len): page = block_table[b, l / page_size] offset = l % page_size // Load K[l, kv_h, :] k_local[4] = kv_cache[page, offset, kv_h, tid*4 : tid*4+4] // coalesced! kf[4] = float(k_local[4]) // Dot product: Q @ K dot = sum(qf[i] * kf[i] for i in 4) // per-thread partial score = warp_reduce_sum(dot) * scale // full score across warp // Online softmax update new_max = max(running_max, score) correction = exp(running_max - new_max) exp_score = exp(score - new_max) running_sum = running_sum * correction + exp_score o_acc[4] = o_acc[4] * correction // Load V[l, kv_h, :] v_local[4] = kv_cache[page, offset, kv_h, D + tid*4 : D + tid*4+4] // coalesced! vf[4] = float(v_local[4]) o_acc[4] += exp_score * vf[4] running_max = new_max // Final output out[b, h, tid*4 : tid*4+4] = bf16(o_acc[4] / running_sum) ``` Wait, this processes one token at a time. Each token requires: - 1 global load of K (128 bytes per warp, coalesced) - 1 global load of V (128 bytes per warp, coalesced) - Computation: dot product (4 muls, reduce), exp, accumulate For L=1024 tokens: 1024 iterations, each loading 256 bytes (K+V) = 256 KB per warp Total KV data per (b, h): 1024 * 256 bytes = 256 KB But with GQA (group_size=4), 4 query heads share the same KV data. This means for group_size=4, we should process all 4 query heads in the same thread block so they can share KV loading! **Optimization: Multiple query heads per thread block sharing KV** For group_size=4: - 1 thread block handles (b, kv_h) and processes all 4 query heads - 4 warps, each warp handles one query head - KV data loaded once by one warp (or cooperatively) and shared But this complicates the design. Let me start simple first and optimize later. Actually, for decode attention, the bottleneck is purely memory bandwidth. The KV cache must be read from DRAM regardless. Whether 4 heads share the load or each head reads independently, the total bytes read from DRAM is the same (unless we can cache KV in shared memory between heads, but L=1024 tokens * 256 bytes = 256KB which is way too big for shared memory). So the simple approach (one warp per (b, h)) is fine for correctness. The memory bandwidth is the bottleneck and it'll be the same regardless. GQA: mapping query head to kv head Let me code this up: ```cpp #include <cuda.h> #include <cuda_bf16.h> #include <cfloat> #include <math.h> static constexpr int WARP_SIZE = 32; __device__ __forceinline__ float warp_reduce_sum(float val) { for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) val += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); return val; } __device__ __forceinline__ float warp_reduce_max(float val) { for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) val = fmaxf(val, __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset)); const int lane_id = threadIdx.x % WARP_SIZE; const int global_warp = blockIdx.x * WARPS_PER_BLOCK + warp_id; const int total_warps = batch * num_heads; if (global_warp >= total_warps) return; const int b = global_warp / num_heads; const int h = global_warp % num_heads; const int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads; const int hkv = h / group_size; const int seq_len = seq_lens[b]; const float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)HEAD_DIM); constexpr int ELEMS_PER_LANE = HEAD_DIM / WARP_SIZE; // Pointers const __nv_bfloat16* q_ptr = query + (b * num_heads + h) * HEAD_DIM; __nv_bfloat16* out_ptr = output + (b * num_heads + h) * HEAD_DIM; // Load Q into registers (fp32 for accumulation) float q[ELEMS_PER_LANE]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { q[i] = __bfloat162float(q_ptr[lane_id * ELEMS_PER_LANE + i]); } // Online softmax accumulators float running_max = -FLT_MAX; float running_sum = 0.0f; float o_acc[ELEMS_PER_LANE] = {0.0f}; // Iterate over pages const int num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size; for (int p = 0; p < num_pages; p++) { const int page_num = block_table[b * max_pages_per_seq + p]; const int page_start = p * page_size; const int page_end = min(page_start + page_size, seq_len); // Iterate over tokens in this page for (int s = page_start; s < page_end; s++) { const int slot = s - page_start; // Pointer to K for this token const __nv_bfloat16* k_ptr = kv_cache + (size_t)page_num * page_size * num_kv_heads * HEAD_DIM * 2 + slot * num_kv_heads * HEAD_DIM * 2 + hkv * HEAD_DIM * 2; // Load K float k[ELEMS_PER_LANE]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { k[i] = __bfloat162float(k_ptr[lane_id * ELEMS_PER_LANE + i]); } // Compute Q @ K (partial per thread) float dot = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { dot += q[i] * k[i]; } // Reduce across warp float score = warp_reduce_sum(dot) * scale; // Online softmax update float new_max = fmaxf(running_max, score); float correction = expf(running_max - new_max); float exp_score = expf(score - new_max); running_sum = running_sum * correction + exp_score; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { o_acc[i] = o_acc[i] * correction; } // Load V const __nv_bfloat16* v_ptr = k_ptr + HEAD_DIM; float v[ELEMS_PER_LANE]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { v[i] = __bfloat162float(v_ptr[lane_id * ELEMS_PER_LANE + i]); } #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { o_acc[i] += exp_score * v[i]; } running_max = new_max; } } // Final normalization float inv_sum = 1.0f / running_sum; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { o_acc[i] *= inv_sum; } // Write output #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < ELEMS_PER_LANE; i++) { out_ptr[lane_id * ELEMS_PER_LANE + i] = __float2bfloat16(o_acc[i]); } } ``` Wait, I need to be careful about the KV cache stride calculation. The layout is (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2). Let me verify: kv_cache layout: (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2) - Dimension strides: (page_size * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2, num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2, head_dim * 2, 1) So for page_num p, slot s, kv_head hkv: offset = p * (page_size * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2) + s * (num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2) + hkv * (head_dim * 2) + d (for K element d) or offset + head_dim + d (for V element d) That matches my code. Let me also double-check the math for online softmax: Standard online softmax: ``` m_0 = -inf, l_0 = 0, O_0 = 0 For j = 1, ..., N: s_j = Q @ K_j / sqrt(d) m_j = max(m_{j-1}, s_j) l_j = l_{j-1} * exp(m_{j-1} - m_j) + exp(s_j - m_j) O_j = O_{j-1} * (l_{j-1}/l_j) * exp(m_{j-1} - m_j) + exp(s_j - m_j)/l_j * V_j ``` Equivalently, accumulate unnormalized: ``` m_j = max(m_{j-1}, s_j) correction = exp(m_{j-1} - m_j) l_j = l_{j-1} * correction + exp(s_j - m_j) O_j = O_{j-1} * correction + exp(s_j - m_j) * V_j ``` Then at the end: O = O_N / l_N This is what I have. Let me verify with a simple example: - Token 1: score = 2.0, V = [1, 0] - m_1 = 2.0, l_1 = exp(2-2) = 1, O_1 = exp(2-2)*[1,0] = [1,0] - Token 2: score = 3.0, V = [0, 1] - m_2 = 3.0, correction = exp(2-3) = exp(-1) - l_2 = 1*exp(-1) + exp(3-3) = exp(-1) + 1 - O_2 = [1,0]*exp(-1) + 1*[0,1] = [exp(-1), 1] - Final: O/l = [exp(-1), 1] / (exp(-1)+1) = [exp(-1)/(exp(-1)+1), 1/(exp(-1)+1)] - Check: softmax = [exp(2), exp(3)] / (exp(2)+exp(3)) = [exp(2)/(exp(2)+exp(3)), exp(3)/(exp(2)+exp(3))] - AV = softmax[0]*[1,0] + softmax[1]*[0,1] = [softmax[0], softmax[1]] - = [exp(2)/(exp(2)+exp(3)), exp(3)/(exp(2)+exp(3))] - My result: [exp(-1)/(exp(-1)+1), 1/(exp(-1)+1)] - exp(-1) = exp(2)/exp(3), so exp(-1)/(exp(-1)+1) = (exp(2)/exp(3)) / (exp(2)/exp(3) + 1) = exp(2)/(exp(2)+exp(3)) ✓ Great, the math checks out. It's well-suited for this kind of kernel. **Triton approach for paged attention decode:** In Triton, I can write a kernel where: - Each program instance handles one (batch, head) pair - Within the program, iterate over KV tokens - Use Triton's load/store operations with proper pointer arithmetic The challenge with Triton for paged attention is the page indirection: we need to look up block_table[b, page_idx] to find the physical page number, then index into kv_cache. This requires a gather operation. Let me think about the Triton kernel structure: ```python @triton.jit def paged_attn_decode_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr, B, H, Hkv, D, P, max_pages, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd, stride_kvn, stride_kvp, stride_kvh, stride_kvd, stride_btb, stride_btp, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, ): pid = tl.program_id(0) b = pid // H h = pid % H group_size = H // Hkv hkv = h // group_size seq_len = tl.load(sl_ptr + b) # Load Q offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) q = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d * stride_qd, mask=offs_d < D) q = q.to(tl.float32) * scale # Online softmax accumulators m_i = tl.full([BLOCK_D], float('-inf'), tl.float32) # wait, m should be scalar # Hmm, this needs more thought ``` Actually, the Triton approach needs some care. Let me think about it more carefully. In Triton, the natural approach would be: - Each program handles one (batch, head) pair - Load Q as a 1D tensor of shape (BLOCK_D,) - Iterate over seq_len in blocks of BLOCK_SEQ tokens - For each block: - Compute page indices and gather K, V from paged cache - Compute QK^T scores - Online softmax update The challenge is that pages break the sequential token access. We need to handle page boundaries. For the QK^T computation in Triton: - Q is (BLOCK_D,) = (D,) - K_block is (BLOCK_SEQ, D) gathered from paged cache - Scores = Q @ K_block^T = (BLOCK_SEQ,) Let me think about how to gather K and V from paged cache in Triton. For a block of tokens [start:end]: - Each token belongs to a specific page - page_idx[l] = (start + l) // P - slot[l] = (start + l) % P - phys_page[l] = block_table[b, page_idx[l]] - K pointer for token l: kv_cache + phys_page[l] * stride_kvn + slot[l] * stride_kvp + hkv * stride_kvh + d * stride_kvd In Triton, I can compute these offsets and use tl.load with the computed pointers. Since different tokens may be on different pages, this is a gather load. ```python # For a block of tokens starting at `start` tok_offs = start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ) # (BLOCK_SEQ,) tok_mask = tok_offs < seq_len page_idx = tok_offs // P # logical page index slot = tok_offs % P # offset within page # Physical page number from block_table phys_page = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_btb + page_idx * stride_btp, mask=tok_mask, other=0) # Pointer to K values k_ptrs = kv_ptr + phys_page[:, None] * stride_kvn + \ slot[:, None] * stride_kvp + \ hkv * stride_kvh + \ offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=(tok_mask[:, None] & (offs_d[None, :] < D)), other=0.0) # scores = Q @ K^T scores = tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1) # (BLOCK_SEQ,) ``` Wait, this won't work directly because `phys_page` is a 1D tensor of shape (BLOCK_SEQ,), and I'm using it to compute 2D pointers. Let me restructure. Actually, in Triton, pointer arithmetic with tensors works element-wise. So: ```python # shape: (BLOCK_SEQ,) phys_page = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_btb + page_idx * stride_btp, mask=tok_mask, other=0) # For K: shape (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) # offset for each (token, dim) pair: # phys_page[token] * stride_kvn + slot[token] * stride_kvp + hkv * stride_kvh + dim * stride_kvd k_base = phys_page * stride_kvn + slot * stride_kvp + hkv * stride_kvh # (BLOCK_SEQ,) k_ptrs = k_base[:, None] + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd # (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) k_ptrs = kv_ptr + k_ptrs ``` This should work! The gather is implicit - each row of the 2D pointer tensor points to a different physical page. But wait, within a block of BLOCK_SEQ consecutive tokens, most will be on the same page (since page_size=16). Only at page boundaries will there be a mix of pages. So for BLOCK_SEQ <= page_size, at most 2 pages are involved. For efficiency, I should use BLOCK_SEQ <= page_size (16). With BLOCK_SEQ=16, each block of tokens is exactly one page (or straddles a boundary). This simplifies the gather. Actually, with BLOCK_SEQ=16 and page_size=16, tokens 0-15 are in page 0, tokens 16-31 in page 1, etc. So each block is exactly one page! The physical page is: page_idx = (start + arange(16)) // 16 = start // 16 (for all tokens in the block) slot = (start + arange(16)) % 16 = arange(16) (for all tokens in the block when start is page-aligned) But start might not be page-aligned if we're processing in blocks of 16... Actually, if we process in blocks of page_size starting from 0, then each block is exactly one page: block 0: tokens 0-15, page_idx=0, slot=0-15 block 1: tokens 16-31, page_idx=1, slot=0-15 etc. So we can iterate over pages directly: ```python for p in range(num_pages): phys_page = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_btb + p * stride_btp) # K for this page: kv_cache[phys_page, :, hkv, :D] # All BLOCK_SEQ tokens have the same phys_page, different slots k_ptrs = kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kvn + offs_slot[:, None] * stride_kvp + hkv * stride_kvh + offs_d[None, :] * stride_kvd k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=...) ``` But wait, the last page might have fewer tokens than page_size. We need to mask: ```python tok_mask = (p * P + offs_slot) < seq_len ``` This is much cleaner! Since page_size = 16 for all shapes, BLOCK_SEQ = 16. But BLOCK_SEQ = 16 might be too small for the QK^T computation. The score vector would be length 16, which is tiny. Let me think... For the attention computation with BLOCK_SEQ = 16: - Load K: (16, D) = (16, 128) bf16 = 4KB - Load V: same - Compute scores: Q @ K^T -> (16,) in fp32 - This is 16 * 128 = 2048 multiply-adds per page The computation per page is small, but the key is that we're memory-bound anyway. The kernel will be dominated by the time to load K and V from DRAM. However, using BLOCK_SEQ = 16 might result in too many iterations for long sequences: - L=4096, P=16 -> 256 iterations - Each iteration loads 2 * 16 * 128 * 2 = 8KB of KV data This should be fine - 256 iterations is not too many. But there's a concern about Triton kernel launch overhead per iteration. Actually, the iterations are within a single kernel launch (the for loop is inside the kernel), so there's no additional launch overhead. OK, let me go with BLOCK_SEQ = 16 (matching page_size) for simplicity. Hmm, but actually I realize there's a subtlety with Triton's auto-vectorization. When loading K for a page, the access pattern is: kv_cache[phys_page, slot, hkv, d] where slot varies from 0-15 and d varies from 0-127. If stride_kvd = 1 (contiguous in the last dimension), then loading a row of K (for one slot) is a contiguous access. Loading across slots requires stride = stride_kvp = num_kv_heads * 2 * head_dim. For Triton, a 2D load like this is fine - it'll be compiled to efficient memory operations. Let me now write the Triton kernel more carefully: ```python import triton import triton.language as tl @triton.jit def paged_attn_decode_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr, H, Hkv, D, P, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_kvn, stride_kvs, stride_kvh, stride_kvd, stride_btb, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SEQ: tl.constexpr, ): pid = tl.program_id(0) b = pid // H h = pid % H group_size = H // Hkv hkv = h // group_size seq_len = tl.load(sl_ptr + b).to(tl.int32) # Dimension offsets offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) # (BLOCK_D,) mask_d = offs_d < D # Load Q: (BLOCK_D,) q = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0) q = q.to(tl.float32) # Online softmax accumulators m_i = float('-inf') # running max (scalar) l_i = 0.0 # running sum (scalar) o_i = tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32) # running output # Slot offsets within a page offs_s = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ) num_pages = (seq_len + P - 1) // P for p in range(num_pages): # Get physical page number phys_page = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_btb + p).to(tl.int32) # Token mask tok_offs = p * P + offs_s tok_mask = tok_offs < seq_len # Load K: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) k_ptrs = (kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kvn + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kvs + hkv * stride_kvh + offs_d[None, :]) k_mask = tok_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :] k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=k_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Compute scores: Q @ K^T -> (BLOCK_SEQ,) scores = tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1) * scale # Mask out-of-range scores scores = tl.where(tok_mask, scores, float('-inf')) # Online softmax update m_j = tl.max(scores) m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, m_j) # Correction factor for previous accumulation correction = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) l_i = l_i * correction # Exp of scores relative to new max exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new) exp_scores = tl.where(tok_mask, exp_scores, 0.0) l_i += tl.sum(exp_scores) o_i = o_i * correction # Load V: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) v_ptrs = k_ptrs + D # V starts at offset D from K in the packed layout v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=k_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Accumulate weighted V o_i += tl.sum(exp_scores[:, None] * v, axis=0) m_i = m_new # Final normalization o_i = o_i / l_i # Store output tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, o_i.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) ``` Wait, I have a problem with the V pointer. The KV cache packs [K|V] in the last dimension, so the stride for V within the same (page, slot, kv_head) tuple is just offset by D. But my `k_ptrs` computation uses `offs_d[None, :]` which ranges from 0 to BLOCK_D-1. For V, I need to access `offs_d[None, :] + D`. So `v_ptrs = kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kvn + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kvs + hkv * stride_kvh + (offs_d[None, :] + D)`. Which is `k_ptrs + D` only if stride_kvd = 1. Let me check: the last dimension of kv_cache is (head_dim * 2) and stride_kvd should be 1 (contiguous). So `k_ptrs + D` should work. But wait, Triton's pointer arithmetic... `k_ptrs` is a tensor of pointers. Adding a scalar `D` to it should offset each pointer by `D * element_size`. But since we're working with bf16 (2 bytes per element), we need to add `D` (in elements, not bytes), which is what Triton does - it works in element units. So `v_ptrs = k_ptrs + D` is correct for stride_kvd = 1. Let me verify this is the case: kv_cache shape: (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2) - stride_kvn = page_size * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 - stride_kvs = num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 - stride_kvh = head_dim * 2 - stride_kvd = 1 Yes, stride_kvd = 1. So `k_ptrs + D` correctly points to V. Actually, there's another issue. I'm loading K with shape (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) where BLOCK_D might be larger than D (when D=64 and BLOCK_D=128). The mask handles this, but the V pointer offset would be wrong because `k_ptrs` already has `offs_d` going up to BLOCK_D-1, and I need V to be at offset D from K start (not BLOCK_D). Hmm, let me think about this more carefully. For D=64, BLOCK_D=128: - K access: k_ptrs[...] with offs_d in [0, 127], masked by offs_d < D=64 - V access: should be at base + D = base + 64, with offsets [0, D-1] So `v_ptrs = k_ptrs + D` with offs_d still going [0, BLOCK_D-1] and mask_d handling the extra. But this means for the K load, we're accessing offsets 0 to 63 (valid K), and for the V load with k_ptrs + D, we're accessing offsets 64 to 127, which maps to kv_cache[..., D:D+64] = V. Wait, that's actually correct! Because: - k_ptrs with offs_d in [0, BLOCK_D-1] covers kv positions 0 to BLOCK_D-1 - v_ptrs = k_ptrs + D means we're accessing kv positions D to D+BLOCK_D-1 - With mask_d = offs_d < D, for V we'd load v_ptrs with mask_d, which means we load positions D to D+D-1 = D to 2D-1 That's exactly V! Great. But there's a subtle issue: when BLOCK_D > D, the v_ptrs with offs_d going to BLOCK_D-1 would access memory at D + BLOCK_D-1 which might be out of bounds of the kv_cache last dimension (which is 2*D). Since BLOCK_D >= D, D + BLOCK_D - 1 >= 2*D - 1, which is exactly the last element. So it's fine as long as BLOCK_D = D. If BLOCK_D > D, then D + BLOCK_D - 1 > 2*D - 1, which is out of bounds! So I need BLOCK_D = D, or I need to handle this differently. For our shapes, D is either 64 or 128. I can either: 1. Template BLOCK_D to match D (dispatch at runtime) 2. Always use BLOCK_D = max(D) = 128 and handle the V pointer more carefully Let me use approach 1: dispatch BLOCK_D based on D. Actually, the simplest approach is to always use BLOCK_D = 128 (max head_dim) and handle both D=64 and D=128 cases. For D=64, the mask will zero out the upper half of the load. For V when D=64 and BLOCK_D=128: - k_ptrs cover offsets [0, 127] in the kv last dim - With mask_d (offs_d < 64), only [0, 63] are loaded for K - v_ptrs = k_ptrs + 64 covers offsets [64, 191] - With mask_d, only [64, 127] are loaded - But the kv last dim is 2*64 = 128, so offsets 128-191 are out of bounds! This is a problem. When D=64, the kv_cache last dim is 128 (2*64). With BLOCK_D=128, loading V with k_ptrs + D would try to access offsets 64+0 to 64+127 = 64 to 191, but the valid range for V is only 64 to 127. So I need to handle D < BLOCK_D carefully. The simplest fix is to compute V pointers independently: ```python v_ptrs = (kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kvn + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kvs + hkv * stride_kvh + D + offs_d[None, :]) ``` With mask_d (offs_d < D), this only accesses D to 2*D-1, which is always valid. The Triton load with mask will not access out-of-bounds memory. Wait, but Triton may still generate memory accesses for masked-out elements depending on the implementation. Let me think... Actually, Triton's `tl.load(ptrs, mask=..., other=0.0)` should handle this correctly - it will not access out-of-bounds memory when the mask is False. The `other` value is used for those positions. But I need to be careful: Triton might still generate vector loads that span valid and invalid addresses. For correctness, the mask must prevent out-of-bounds reads. For safety, let me just use BLOCK_D = 128 always but compute V pointers separately: ```python v_ptrs = (kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kvn + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kvs + hkv * stride_kvh + D + offs_d[None, :]) v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=k_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) ``` With mask_d limiting offs_d to < D, this should be safe. Hmm, but I need to double-check: does Triton guarantee no out-of-bounds memory access when mask is False? According to Triton docs, `tl.load` with mask guarantees safety - it won't access out-of-bounds addresses. So this should be fine. OK, let me finalize the kernel and write the solution. One more thing: I should think about performance optimizations: 1. **Use a larger BLOCK_SEQ for better memory throughput**: Instead of iterating page by page, I could process multiple pages at once. But since page_size=16 is small, the overhead is minimal. 2. **Avoid repeated block_table lookups**: For page p, I look up block_table once. This is fine. 3. **Memory access pattern**: K and V loads are gathered across pages. Within a page, the access is sequential in the slot dimension, which should be cache-friendly. 4. **Grid size**: For shape 2 (B=32, H=32), we have 1024 program instances. Triton should handle this well. 5. **Using `tl.dot` for matrix multiplication**: For the QK^T computation, `tl.sum(q * k, axis=1)` is a reduction. Using `tl.dot` might be faster but requires specific block sizes. For D=128, BLOCK_D=128, this might not align with Triton's dot product requirements. Actually, for Triton, `tl.dot` requires both operands to be 2D and the K dimension to match. In our case: - q: (BLOCK_D,) - need to reshape to (1, BLOCK_D) - k: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) - scores = tl.dot(k, q[None, :]) would give (BLOCK_SEQ, 1) -> squeeze to (BLOCK_SEQ,) Wait, `tl.dot(a, b)` where a is (M, K) and b is (K, N) gives (M, N). So: - q as (1, D) and k as (BLOCK_SEQ, D) - scores = tl.dot(k, q_transposed) where q is (D, 1) - scores = tl.dot(k, q[:, None]) doesn't work because k is (BLOCK_SEQ, D) and q[:, None] is (D, 1) - So tl.dot(k, q_t) = (BLOCK_SEQ, D) @ (D, 1) = (BLOCK_SEQ, 1) Hmm, Triton's tl.dot might require specific block sizes. Let me check if the simpler `tl.sum(q * k, axis=1)` works efficiently. For memory-bound decode, the compute efficiency of the dot product doesn't matter much. Actually, you know what, let me just go with Triton. It's the safer choice and should work well for this memory-bound kernel. I can always optimize further if needed. Let me also think about one more optimization: **process multiple query heads per program for GQA**. With GQA, group_size query heads share the same KV head. If I process them together: - Load K and V once - Compute QK^T for each of the group_size query heads - This reduces KV cache reads by group_size For group_size=4 (most of our shapes), this means 4x less KV cache traffic! This is a significant optimization. Let me restructure the kernel: ``` Each program handles (batch, kv_head) -> all group_size query heads ``` Within the kernel: - Load K and V for all tokens (shared across query heads) - For each query head in the group: - Load Q - Compute scores, online softmax, accumulate output - Write output But this requires more registers/shared memory. Let me think about whether it's worth it. For shape 1: B=8, H=32, Hkv=8, group_size=4 - Without GQA sharing: 8*32 = 256 program instances - With GQA sharing: 8*8 = 64 program instances, each doing 4x more work on Q The total KV reads are the same (B * L * Hkv * D * 2 bytes). The difference is that with sharing, each program loads KV once and uses it for 4 query heads. Without sharing, each of the 4 query heads loads the same KV data independently. Since the kernel is memory-bound, reducing total memory reads by 4x is a huge win! But... the KV data (K and V for all tokens) is too large to keep in shared memory. For L=1024 tokens with D=128: - K: 1024 * 128 * 2 = 256 KB - V: same That's way too much for shared memory. So we'd still need to stream K and V from DRAM for each query head. The total DRAM traffic is the same. Wait, but if we process all query heads in the same kernel, we could keep K and V in L2 cache between heads. The first head would bring KV into L2, and subsequent heads would hit L2. This is only true if the L2 is large enough to hold the KV data. RTX PRO 6000 has a large L2 cache. Let me check... RTX 4090 has 72MB L2. RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell might have even more. For L=1024, Hkv=8, D=128: KV = 2 * 1024 * 8 * 128 * 2 = 4 MB. That fits easily in L2! For L=4096: KV = 2 * 4096 * 8 * 128 * 2 = 16 MB. Still fits in L2 for most GPUs. So the GQA sharing approach could significantly reduce DRAM traffic. But it requires careful kernel design. For the Triton kernel with GQA sharing: - Each program handles (batch, kv_head) - Within the program, iterate over tokens (streaming K and V) - For each token, load K and V once, compute QK^T for all group_size query heads ```python @triton.jit def paged_attn_decode_gqa_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr, H, Hkv, D, P, GROUP_SIZE, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_kvn, stride_kvs, stride_kvh, stride_kvd, stride_btb, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SEQ: tl.constexpr, ): pid = tl.program_id(0) b = pid // Hkv hkv = pid % Hkv seq_len = tl.load(sl_ptr + b).to(tl.int32) offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) mask_d = offs_d < D offs_s = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ) # Load Q for all query heads in this group # q shape: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D) # Each query head h = hkv * GROUP_SIZE + g q = tl.zeros([GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D], tl.float32) for g in range(GROUP_SIZE): h = hkv * GROUP_SIZE + g q_g = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0) q[g, :] = q_g.to(tl.float32) # Online softmax accumulators for each query head m_i = tl.full([GROUP_SIZE], float('-inf'), tl.float32) l_i = tl.zeros([GROUP_SIZE], tl.float32) o_i = tl.zeros([GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D], tl.float32) num_pages = (seq_len + P - 1) // P for p in range(num_pages): phys_page = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_btb + p).to(tl.int32) tok_offs = p * P + offs_s tok_mask = tok_offs < seq_len # Load K: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) k_ptrs = kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kvn + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kvs + hkv * stride_kvh + offs_d[None, :] k_mask = tok_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :] k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=k_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Compute scores for all query heads: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ) # q: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), k: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)) * scale # (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ) scores = tl.where(tok_mask[None, :], scores, float('-inf')) # Online softmax m_j = tl.max(scores, axis=1) # (GROUP_SIZE,) m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, m_j) correction = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) # (GROUP_SIZE,) l_i = l_i * correction exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new[:, None]) exp_scores = tl.where(tok_mask[None, :], exp_scores, 0.0) l_i += tl.sum(exp_scores, axis=1) o_i = o_i * correction[:, None] # Load V: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) v_ptrs = kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kvn + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kvs + hkv * stride_kvh + (D + offs_d[None, :]) v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=k_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Accumulate: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ) @ (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) -> (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D) o_i += tl.dot(exp_scores, v) m_i = m_new o_i = o_i / l_i[:, None] # Store output for each query head for g in range(GROUP_SIZE): h = hkv * GROUP_SIZE + g tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, o_i[g, :].to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) ``` Hmm wait, there's an issue with `tl.trans(k)`. Triton might not support transposing a 2D tensor in the middle of a kernel efficiently. Let me check... Actually, Triton does support `tl.trans()` (or `tl.view` with reordering). But `tl.dot` in Triton has specific requirements: - Both inputs must be 2D - The inner dimensions must match - Specific block sizes may be required for hardware dot products For `tl.dot(q, k.T)`: q is (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), k.T is (BLOCK_D, BLOCK_SEQ). Result: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ). This is fine if GROUP_SIZE and BLOCK_SEQ are reasonable sizes. But wait, GROUP_SIZE might be 4 or 8 (from our shapes), and BLOCK_SEQ=16. These are very small for tl.dot which might be designed for larger matrices. The overhead might outweigh the benefit. Let me reconsider. For small GROUP_SIZE (4-8) and small BLOCK_SEQ (16), the matrix multiplications are tiny. The overhead of tl.dot setup might dominate. Alternative: compute scores using element-wise operations: ```python # q: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), k: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) # scores: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ) = sum(q[g,d] * k[s,d], d) scores = tl.sum(q[:, None, :] * k[None, :, :], axis=2) # broadcasts to (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D), then reduce ``` But this creates a 3D intermediate tensor which might use too much memory. For GROUP_SIZE=4, BLOCK_SEQ=16, BLOCK_D=128: 4 * 16 * 128 * 4 bytes = 32 KB. That's a lot of shared memory or register pressure. Hmm, maybe I should stick with the simpler approach: one program per (batch, query_head), no GQA sharing. The memory bandwidth savings from GQA sharing require KV to stay in L2 between heads, which is not guaranteed. Let me finalize the kernel design: ```python import torch import triton import triton.language as tl import math @triton.jit def paged_attn_decode_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr, H: tl.constexpr, Hkv: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, stride_q_batch, stride_q_head, stride_kv_block, stride_kv_slot, stride_kv_head, stride_bt_batch, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SEQ: tl.constexpr, # = P, process one page at a time ): pid = tl.program_id(0) b = pid // H h = pid % H group_size = H // Hkv hkv = h // group_size seq_len = tl.load(sl_ptr + b).to(tl.int32) if seq_len == 0: # Write zeros offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) mask_d = offs_d < D tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_q_batch + h * stride_q_head + offs_d, tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) return offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) mask_d = offs_d < D # Load Q q = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_q_batch + h * stride_q_head + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Accumulators m_i = float('-inf') l_i = 0.0 o_i = tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32) offs_s = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ) num_pages = (seq_len + P - m_new) if m_i != float('-inf') else 0.0 exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new) exp_scores = tl.where(tok_mask, exp_scores, 0.0) l_i = l_i * correction + tl.sum(exp_scores) o_i = o_i * correction # Load V v_ptrs = (kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kv_block + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kv_slot + hkv * stride_kv_head + D + offs_d[None, :]) v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=k_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) o_i += tl.sum(exp_scores[:, None] * v, axis=0) m_i = m_new # Normalize and store o_i = o_i / l_i tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_q_batch + h * stride_q_head + offs_d, o_i.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) ``` Hmm, there's a problem with `correction = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) if m_i != float('-inf') else 0.0`. When m_i = -inf: - correction = exp(-inf - m_new) = 0 - l_i = 0 * 0 + sum(exp_scores) = sum(exp_scores) ✓ - o_i = 0 * 0 = 0 ✓ So actually, `correction = tl.exp(m_i - m_new)` gives exp(-inf - m_new) = 0, which is correct! The issue is that exp(-inf - x) should be 0 mathematically, but in floating point, -inf - x = -inf, and exp(-inf) = 0. So this is fine! But wait, what if m_i = m_new? The grid size should be: - grid = (B * H, 1, 1) for the non-GQA approach But B and H vary per shape. I can compute the grid size dynamically. For the `triton.cdiv` or manual computation: grid = (B * H + 0, 1, 1). Since each program handles exactly one (b, h) pair, I need exactly B * H programs. But if I have multiple warps per block (WARPS_PER_BLOCK > 1), I'd need fewer blocks. Let me just use 1 program per (b, h) and let Triton handle the block scheduling. In Triton, each program_id is one "thread block" essentially, and Triton decides the thread count. Actually, in Triton, the `num_warps` parameter controls how many warps are used per program instance. So with `num_warps=4`, each program instance uses 4 warps = 128 threads. The total number of programs is still B * H. For memory-bound kernels, more programs (higher occupancy) is better. With `num_warps=1` or `num_warps=2`, we can have more concurrent programs. But each program needs enough threads to efficiently load memory. For BLOCK_D=128 with `num_warps=4` (128 threads): - Each warp handles 128/4 = 32 elements of the dot product - Wait, that's not how Triton works. Triton distributes the block dimensions across all threads. Actually, in Triton, the programming model is different from CUDA. You don't manually assign threads to work. Instead, you write the algorithm at the block level, and Triton auto-parallelizes across threads within the block. For a load like `tl.load(ptr + offs_d)` where offs_d has shape (128,), Triton distributes this across all threads in the block. With 4 warps (128 threads), each thread handles 1 element. OK, so the number of warps affects how much work each thread does, which affects register pressure and shared memory usage. For BLOCK_D=128 and BLOCK_SEQ=16: - K load: (16, 128) = 2048 elements. With 4 warps (128 threads), each thread handles 16 elements. - Q load: (128,) = 128 elements. Each thread handles 1 element. This should work fine with 4 warps. Let me set `num_warps=4` for good occupancy. Now, let me think about the `num_stages` parameter. This controls software pipelining in Triton. For memory-bound kernels, higher `num_stages` can help overlap memory loads with computation. Let me try `num_stages=3` or `4`. OK, let me write the code now. I've been thinking long enough. Let me also check: does the Triton `tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1)` correctly compute the dot product between Q and each row of K? - q[None, :] has shape (1, BLOCK_D) - k has shape (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) - q[None, :] * k broadcasts to (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) - tl.sum(..., axis=1) reduces over axis 1 -> (BLOCK_SEQ,) Yes, this gives scores[s] = sum_d q[d] * k[s, d], which is Q @ K^T. Correct. And `tl.sum(exp_scores[:, None] * v, axis=0)`: - exp_scores[:, None] has shape (BLOCK_SEQ, 1) - v has shape (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) - Product: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) - Sum over axis 0: (BLOCK_D,) This gives sum_s exp_scores[s] * v[s, d], which is the weighted sum of V. Correct. Now let me write the full solution.py: ```python """Paged attention decode kernel using Triton. Single-query decode with paged KV cache, online softmax in fp32. """ import math import torch import torch.nn as nn import triton import triton.language as tl OP_TYPE = "attention" SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"] HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"] BATCH = 8 NUM_HEADS = 32 NUM_KV_HEADS = 8 HEAD_DIM = 128 SEQ_LEN = 1024 PAGE_SIZE = 16 @triton.jit def _paged_attn_decode_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr, num_heads: tl.constexpr, num_kv_heads: tl.constexpr, head_dim: tl.constexpr, page_size: tl.constexpr, stride_q_b, stride_q_h, stride_kv_block, stride_kv_slot, stride_kv_head, stride_bt_b, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SEQ: tl.constexpr, ): pid = tl.program_id(0) total_heads = num_heads # We launch B * H programs b = pid // total_heads h = pid % total_heads group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads hkv = h // group_size seq_len = tl.load(sl_ptr + b).to(tl.int32) offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) mask_d = offs_d < head_dim # Handle empty sequence if seq_len == 0: tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_q_b + h * stride_q_h + offs_d, tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32).to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) return # Load Q q = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_q_b + h * stride_q_h + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Online softmax accumulators m_i = float('-inf') l_i = float(0.0) o_i = tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32) offs_s = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ) num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) // page_size for p_idx in range(num_pages): phys_page = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_bt_b + p_idx).to(tl.int32) tok_offs = p_idx * page_size + offs_s tok_mask = tok_offs < seq_len # Load K: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) k_ptrs = (kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kv_block + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kv_slot + hkv * stride_kv_head + offs_d[None, :]) k_load_mask = tok_mask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :] k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=k_load_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Q @ K^T -> (BLOCK_SEQ,) scores = tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1) * scale scores = tl.where(tok_mask, scores, float('-inf')) # Online softmax m_j = tl.max(scores) m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, m_j) correction = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) exp_scores = tl.exp(scores - m_new) exp_scores = tl.where(tok_mask, exp_scores, 0.0) l_i = l_i * correction + tl.sum(exp_scores) o_i = o_i * correction # Load V v_ptrs = (kv_ptr + phys_page * stride_kv_block + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kv_slot + hkv * stride_kv_head + head_dim + offs_d[None, :]) v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=k_load_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) o_i += tl.sum(exp_scores[:, None] * v, axis=0) m_i = m_new # Normalize and store o_i = o_i * (1.0 / l_i) tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_q_b + h * stride_q_h + offs_d, o_i.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) class Model(nn.Module): def __init__(self, batch, num_heads, num_kv_heads, head_dim, seq_len, page_size): super().__init__() assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0 self.batch = batch self.num_heads = num_heads self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads self.head_dim = head_dim self.seq_len = seq_len self.page_size = page_size self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim) self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False) def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens): B, H, D = query.shape Hkv = self.num_kv_heads P = self.page_size out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device) BLOCK_D = triton.next_power_of_2(D) # 128 for D=128, 128 for D=64 (over-provision) # Actually, for D=64, BLOCK_D should be 64 to avoid out-of-bounds # But we mask, so it's fine... except for V pointer offset # Let me use BLOCK_D = max(D, 64) rounded up to power of 2 BLOCK_D = max(triton.next_power_of_2(D), 64) BLOCK_SEQ = P # Process one page at a time grid = (B * H,) _paged_attn_decode_kernel[grid]( query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, out, num_heads=H, num_kv_heads=Hkv, head_dim=D, page_size=P, stride_q_b=query.stride(0), stride_q_h=query.stride(1), stride_kv_block=kv_cache.stride(0), stride_kv_slot=kv_cache.stride(1), stride_kv_head=kv_cache.stride(2), stride_bt_b=block_table.stride(0), scale=self.scale, BLOCK_D=BLOCK_D, BLOCK_SEQ=BLOCK_SEQ, num_warps=4, num_stages=3, ) return out def get_inputs(): B = BATCH H = NUM_HEADS Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS D = HEAD_DIM L = SEQ_LEN P = PAGE_SIZE pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64) query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1 kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1 perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[:B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int() block_table = perm.contiguous() seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32) return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens] def get_init_inputs(): return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE] ``` Wait, I have a concern. Let me also think about the solution.py structure: ```python """Custom paged attention decode kernel using Triton.""" import math import torch import torch.nn as nn import triton import triton.language as tl # Module-level shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py) BATCH = 8 NUM_HEADS = 32 NUM_KV_HEADS = 8 HEAD_DIM = 128 SEQ_LEN = 1024 PAGE_SIZE = 16 OP_TYPE = "attention" SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"] HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"] @triton.jit def _paged_attn_decode_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr, H: tl.constexpr, Hkv: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_kv0, stride_kv1, stride_kv2, stride_bt0, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SEQ: tl.constexpr, ): pid = tl.program_id(0) b = pid // H h = pid % H group = H // Hkv hkv = h // group L = tl.load(sl_ptr + b).to(tl.int32) offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) mask_d = offs_d < D if L == 0: tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32).to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) return # Load query q = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0) q = q.to(tl.float32) # Accumulators for online softmax mi = float('-inf') li = float(0.0) oi = tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32) offs_s = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ) npages = (L + P - 1) // P for pi in range(npages): pp = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_bt0 + pi).to(tl.int32) toffs = pi * P + offs_s tmask = toffs < L # K pointers kptrs = (kv_ptr + pp * stride_kv0 + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kv1 + hkv * stride_kv2 + offs_d[None, :]) kmask = tmask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :] k = tl.load(kptrs, mask=kmask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # QK^T s = tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1) * scale s = tl.where(tmask, s, float('-inf')) # Online softmax update mj = tl.max(s) mnew = tl.maximum(mi, mj) corr = tl.exp(mi - mnew) es = tl.exp(s - mnew) es = tl.where(tmask, es, 0.0) li = li * corr + tl.sum(es) oi = oi * corr # V pointers vptrs = kptrs + D v = tl.load(vptrs, mask=kmask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) oi += tl.sum(es[:, None] * v, axis=0) mi = mnew oi = oi * (1.0 / li) tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, oi.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) class Model(nn.Module): def __init__(self, batch, num_heads, num_kv_heads, head_dim, seq_len, page_size): super().__init__() assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0 self.batch = batch self.num_heads = num_heads self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads self.head_dim = head_dim self.seq_len = seq_len self.page_size = page_size self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim) self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False) def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens): B, H, D = query.shape Hkv = self.num_kv_heads P = self.page_size out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=query.device) BLOCK_D = triton.next_power_of_2(D) BLOCK_SEQ = P grid = (B * H,) _paged_attn_decode_kernel[grid]( query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, out, H=H, Hkv=Hkv, D=D, P=P, stride_qb=query.stride(0), stride_qh=query.stride(1), stride_kv0=kv_cache.stride(0), stride_kv1=kv_cache.stride(1), stride_kv2=kv_cache.stride(2), stride_bt0=block_table.stride(0), scale=self.scale, BLOCK_D=BLOCK_D, BLOCK_SEQ=BLOCK_SEQ, ) return out def get_inputs(): B = BATCH H = NUM_HEADS Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS D = HEAD_DIM L = SEQ_LEN P = PAGE_SIZE pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64) query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1 kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1 perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[:B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int() block_table = perm.contiguous() seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32) return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens] def get_init_inputs(): return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE] ``` Wait, I have a potential issue. The loop bound `npages` is a runtime scalar, which Triton handles. But there's a subtlety: Triton's loop unrolling/optimization requires knowing the trip count at compile time for best results. With a dynamic trip count, Triton will generate a loop with the computed bound. This is fine but might not be as optimized. For our shapes, the maximum num_pages is (4096 + 15) // 16 = 256. This is not too large for a loop. OK, let me also think about the `tl.load` for the page number. This is a scalar load from block_table, which is in global memory. For D=128: kptrs points to K (elements 0 to 127 in the last dim), kptrs + D points to V (elements 128 to 255). I can potentially use HMMA (tensor core) instructions for the QK^T computation But the development time is longer. Let me start with Triton and switch if performance is insufficient. One more optimization I want to add: instead of loading K and V separately (two global memory accesses), I can load the packed [K|V] array once and split in registers. This halves the number of global loads. For D=128, the packed [K|V] is 256 bf16 = 512 bytes per token per kv_head. Loading all 256 at once and splitting into K (0:128) and V (128:256) is more efficient than two separate loads. In Triton: ```python # Load packed KV: (BLOCK_SEQ, 2*D) kv_ptrs = (kv_ptr + pp * stride_kv0 + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kv1 + hkv * stride_kv2 + offs_kv[None, :]) # offs_kv goes from 0 to 2*D-1 kv = tl.load(kv_ptrs, mask=kv_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Split k = kv[:, :D] v = kv[:, D:] ``` But this requires BLOCK_KV = 2*D as the block size, which might be too large for Triton's block size constraints. Also fine. The advantage: one coalesced load of 2*D per token instead of two loads of D. This can improve memory throughput because: 1. One load instruction instead of two 2. For the online softmax, the critical operations are: 1. `mi - mnew`: this can be 0 (when mi == mnew) or very negative (when mi << mnew) 2. `exp(mi - mnew)`: when mi - mnew is very negative, this is 0. When 0, this is 1. 3. `exp(s - mnew)`: s <= mnew, so s - mnew <= 0. exp is in [0, 1]. These should all be fine with fp32 precision. OK, let me write the code. I'll be methodical about it. +"""Custom paged attention decode kernel using Triton.
+
+Single-query decode with paged KV cache, online softmax in fp32.
+One Triton program per (batch, query_head). GQA heads share KV via L2 cache.
+"""
+import math
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+OP_TYPE = "attention"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
+
+BATCH = 8
+NUM_HEADS = 32
+NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
+HEAD_DIM = 128
+SEQ_LEN = 1024
+PAGE_SIZE = 16
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _paged_attn_decode_kernel(
+    q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr,
+    H: tl.constexpr,
+    Hkv: tl.constexpr,
+    D: tl.constexpr,
+    P: tl.constexpr,
+    stride_qb,
+    stride_qh,
+    stride_kv0,
+    stride_kv1,
+    stride_kv2,
+    stride_bt0,
+    scale,
+    BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_SEQ: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    b = pid // H
+    h = pid % H
+    group = H // Hkv
+    hkv = h // group
+
+    L = tl.load(sl_ptr + b).to(tl.int32)
+
+    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
+    mask_d = offs_d < D
+
+    if L == 0:
+        tl.store(
+            out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d,
+            tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32).to(tl.bfloat16),
+            mask=mask_d,
+        )
+        return
+
+    q = tl.load(
+        q_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0
+    ).to(tl.float32)
+
+    mi = float("-inf")
+    li = float(0.0)
+    oi = tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32)
+
+    offs_s = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ)
+    npages = (L + P - 1) // P
+
+    for pi in range(npages):
+        pp = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_bt0 + pi).to(tl.int32)
+
+        toffs = pi * P + offs_s
+        tmask = toffs < L
+
+        k_ptrs = (
+            kv_ptr
+            + pp * stride_kv0
+            + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kv1
+            + hkv * stride_kv2
+            + offs_d[None, :]
+        )
+        km = tmask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :]
+        k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=km, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+        s = tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1) * scale
+        s = tl.where(tmask, s, float("-inf"))
+
+        mj = tl.max(s)
+        mnew = tl.maximum(mi, mj)
+        corr = tl.exp(mi - mnew)
+        es = tl.exp(s - mnew)
+        es = tl.where(tmask, es, 0.0)
+
+        li = li * corr + tl.sum(es)
+        oi = oi * corr
+
+        v_ptrs = k_ptrs + D
+        v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=km, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+        oi += tl.sum(es[:, None] * v, axis=0)
+        mi = mnew
+
+    oi = oi * (1.0 / li)
+    tl.store(
+        out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d,
+        oi.to(tl.bfloat16),
+        mask=mask_d,
+    )
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    def __init__(self, batch, num_heads, num_kv_heads, head_dim, seq_len, page_size):
+        super().__init__()
+        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0
+        self.batch = batch
+        self.num_heads = num_heads
+        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
+        self.head_dim = head_dim
+        self.seq_len = seq_len
+        self.page_size = page_size
+        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
+        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
+        self.register_buffer(
+            "_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False
+        )
+
+    def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens):
+        B, H, D = query.shape
+        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
+        P = self.page_size
+
+        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=query.device)
+
+        BLOCK_D = triton.next_power_of_2(D)
+        BLOCK_SEQ = P
+
+        num_warps = 4
+        if BLOCK_D <= 64:
+            num_warps = 2
+
+        grid = (B * H,)
+        _paged_attn_decode_kernel[grid](
+            query,
+            kv_cache,
+            block_table,
+            seq_lens,
+            out,
+            H=H,
+            Hkv=Hkv,
+            D=D,
+            P=P,
+            stride_qb=query.stride(0),
+            stride_qh=query.stride(1),
+            stride_kv0=kv_cache.stride(0),
+            stride_kv1=kv_cache.stride(1),
+            stride_kv2=kv_cache.stride(2),
+            stride_bt0=block_table.stride(0),
+            scale=self.scale,
+            BLOCK_D=BLOCK_D,
+            BLOCK_SEQ=BLOCK_SEQ,
+            num_warps=num_warps,
+            num_stages=3,
+        )
+
+        return out
+
+
+def get_inputs():
+    B = BATCH
+    H = NUM_HEADS
+    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
+    D = HEAD_DIM
+    L = SEQ_LEN
+    P = PAGE_SIZE
+
+    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
+    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)
+
+    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
+    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
+    perm = (
+        torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq]
+        .reshape(B, pages_per_seq)
+        .int()
+    )
+    block_table = perm.contiguous()
+    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)
+
+    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]
+
+
+def get_init_inputs():
+    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]
args

That's actually not bad! But the benchmark only counts the unique KV data (33.5 MB) for the bandwidth calculation, so the peak_fraction appears low. This means the issue is that my kernel reads KV data redundantly for GQA heads, and the benchmark formula counts only unique bytes. To improve peak_fraction, I need to either: 1. Share KV data across GQA heads (so it's only read once) 2. Or process all GQA heads in one program to avoid redundant reads The GQA sharing approach is critical for performance! Let me redesign the kernel to share KV across GQA heads. **GQA-shared kernel design:** Grid: (B * Hkv, 1, 1) - one program per (batch, kv_head) Each program: 1. Iterates over pages, loading K and V for its kv_head 2. For each page, computes QK^T for all group_size query heads 3. Maintains separate softmax accumulators for each query head 4. Writes output for all group_size query heads The loop structure: ``` for each page: load K, V # shared across all query heads in the group for g in range(group_size): q = load Q[b, hkv*group_size + g] scores = QK^T(q, K) online softmax update for head g accumulate weighted V for head g ``` Or better, vectorize across query heads: ``` # Load all Q heads upfront for g in range(group_size): q[g] = load Q[b, hkv*group_size + g] # Process pages for each page: load K, V for g in range(group_size): scores = QK^T(q[g], K) update accumulators ``` In Triton, loading Q for all group_size heads at once: ```python # Q: (GROUP_SIZE, D) in fp32 q = tl.zeros([GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D], tl.float32) for g in range(GROUP_SIZE): h = hkv * GROUP_SIZE + g q[g] = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) ``` The accumulators: ```python mi = tl.full([GROUP_SIZE], float('-inf'), tl.float32) li = tl.zeros([GROUP_SIZE], tl.float32) oi = tl.zeros([GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D], tl.float32) ``` For each page: ```python k = load K # (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) v = load V # (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) for g in range(GROUP_SIZE): scores = tl.sum(q[g][None, :] * k, axis=1) * scale # (BLOCK_SEQ,) # online softmax update for head g ... oi[g] += weighted sum of V ``` The issue is that with GROUP_SIZE=8 (shape 3), this is a lot of register pressure: - q: 8 * 128 = 1024 fp32 values - oi: 8 * 128 = 1024 fp32 values - mi, li: 8 fp32 each - K: 16 * 128 = 2048 fp32 values - V: 16 * 128 = 2048 fp32 values - Plus intermediates Total: ~5000+ fp32 values = 20 KB. With 128 threads, that's ~40 values per thread. At 4 bytes each, 160 bytes per thread, or 40 registers per thread. That's high but feasible (GPUs have up to 255 registers per thread). Actually, the Triton compiler might spill to local memory if register pressure is too high. Let me try and see. But there's a bigger issue: for GROUP_SIZE=4 or 8, the inner loop over query heads within the page loop adds overhead. And for each query head, we need a separate QK^T computation. Alternative: vectorize across query heads using 2D operations: ```python # q: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D) # k: (BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) # scores: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ) = q @ k.T scores = tl.sum(q[:, None, :] * k[None, :, :], axis=2) * scale ``` This computes all GROUP_SIZE * BLOCK_SEQ scores at once. But the intermediate tensor (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ, BLOCK_D) might be too large: - 8 * 16 * 128 = 16384 fp32 = 64 KB - that's way too much for registers! So I can't vectorize across query heads with a 3D intermediate. I need the loop. Let me try the loop approach and see if it works. If the kernel compiles and runs correctly, the performance should be much better because KV is only read once per (batch, kv_head) instead of group_size times. Actually, wait. Let me reconsider. Even with fewer programs, it should be faster because it reduces DRAM traffic by group_size. **Quick optimization 2: Pack K and V into one load** Instead of two separate loads for K and V, load the packed KV once and split in registers. This halves the number of load instructions. **Quick optimization 3: Use tl.dot for the QK^T computation** For the QK^T computation with GQA sharing: - q: (GROUP_SIZE, D) in bf16 - k: (BLOCK_SEQ, D) in bf16 - scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)) * scale -> (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SEQ) tl.dot maps to tensor cores and is faster than element-wise multiply + reduce. But tl.dot has alignment requirements: both dimensions need to be multiples of 16. GROUP_SIZE=4 or 8 is fine. D=128 is fine. BLOCK_SEQ=16 is fine. Let me try this approach! OK, let me write a new version with these optimizations: 1. GQA sharing (one program per (batch, kv_head)) 2. Pack K and V load 3. Use tl.dot for batched QK^T Here's the plan: ```python @triton.jit def _paged_attn_gqa_kernel( q_ptr, kv_ptr, bt_ptr, sl_ptr, out_ptr, H: tl.constexpr, Hkv: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, GROUP: tl.constexpr, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_kv0, stride_kv1, stride_kv2, stride_bt0, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_SEQ: tl.constexpr, ): pid = tl.program_id(0) b = pid // Hkv hkv = pid % Hkv L = tl.load(sl_ptr + b).to(tl.int32) offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) mask_d = offs_d < D if L == 0: for g in range(GROUP): h = hkv * GROUP + g tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) return # Load all GROUP query heads q = tl.zeros([GROUP, BLOCK_D], tl.float32) for g in range(GROUP): h = hkv * GROUP + g q[g] = tl.load(q_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, mask=mask_d, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Accumulators mi = tl.full([GROUP], float('-inf'), tl.float32) li = tl.zeros([GROUP], tl.float32) oi = tl.zeros([GROUP, BLOCK_D], tl.float32) offs_s = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SEQ) npages = (L + P - 1) // P for pi in range(npages): pp = tl.load(bt_ptr + b * stride_bt0 + pi).to(tl.int32) toffs = pi * P + offs_s tmask = toffs < L # Load K k_ptrs = kv_ptr + pp * stride_kv0 + offs_s[:, None] * stride_kv1 + hkv * stride_kv2 + offs_d[None, :] km = tmask[:, None] & mask_d[None, :] k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=km, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Compute scores for all query heads for g in range(GROUP): scores = tl.sum(q[g][None, :] * k, axis=1) * scale scores = tl.where(tmask, scores, float('-inf')) mj = tl.max(scores) mnew = tl.maximum(mi[g], mj) corr = tl.exp(mi[g] - mnew) es = tl.exp(scores - mnew) es = tl.where(tmask, es, 0.0) li[g] = li[g] * corr + tl.sum(es) oi[g] = oi[g] * corr # Load V v_ptrs = k_ptrs + D v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=km, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) oi[g] += tl.sum(es[:, None] * v, axis=0) mi[g] = mnew # Store outputs for g in range(GROUP): h = hkv * GROUP + g oi[g] = oi[g] * (1.0 / li[g]) tl.store(out_ptr + b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh + offs_d, oi[g].to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d) ``` Wait, I'm loading V inside the loop over g, which means V is loaded GROUP times per page! That defeats the purpose of GQA sharing. Let me load V outside the loop: ```python for pi in range(npages): # Load K and V once k = tl.load(k_ptrs, ...) v = tl.load(v_ptrs, ...) for g in range(GROUP): scores = tl.sum(q[g] * k, ...) # softmax update for head g using the same k and v oi[g] += weighted sum of v ``` This is the correct structure: K and V loaded once, used for all GROUP query heads. But there's a register pressure concern: keeping both K (BLOCK_SEQ * BLOCK_D) and V (BLOCK_SEQ * BLOCK_D) in registers while also processing GROUP query heads. K: 16 * 128 = 2048 fp32 = 8 KB V: 16 * 128 = 2048 fp32 = 8 KB q: GROUP * 128 = 4 * 128 = 512 fp32 = 2 KB (for GROUP=4) oi: GROUP * 128 = 512 fp32 = 2 KB mi: GROUP = 4 fp32 li: GROUP = 4 fp32 intermediates: scores (16), es (16), etc. Total: ~20 KB of register data per program. With 128 threads (4 warps), that's ~160 bytes per thread = ~40 registers per thread. Feasible. For GROUP=8: q = 4 KB, oi = 4 KB, total = ~26 KB. That's ~52 registers per thread with 128 threads. Still feasible but getting tight. Let me try this approach. But wait, I also want to keep the option of launching more programs.
